Northeast Remittance Issues

The Pseudo-Organization Announces Exchange Rules and Guidelines / Mail with the Words "Pseudo-State" is Found in the Ping City

Beiping Correspondence: Since the resumption of postal remittances in the Northeast, there have been many mails sent from Beiping to the eastern provinces in recent days. However, some envelopes still have the words "Manchukuo" written on them. Because this writing contains the meaning of recognizing the pseudo-organization, the post office cannot collect and deliver them. If there are no such words and sufficient domestic stamps of 5 cents are affixed, they can be sent as usual. As for the mail entering the Guan from the eastern provinces, the envelopes actually have "Manchukuo" stamps of 4 cents affixed, and no special stamps are affixed. The post office has also not imposed fines for insufficient postage according to the insufficient postage method. After inspection of the envelope, there is a large rectangular stamp, which reads "The invalid stamps affixed to the letter have been compensated by this office," and the lower section states "Qinhuangdao Exchange and Transfer Bureau." This means that although no special stamps are affixed to the letter, it can still be received. As for the resumption of exchange inside and outside the Guan, it is decided to start on the first day of next month. Regarding the detailed rules of exchange, our side has not officially announced them. According to news from outside the Guan, the Postal and Telecommunications Department of the pseudo-Ministry of Transportation has now formulated the exchange rules, which were announced by the pseudo-Ministry on the 11th of this month, and stipulates that all recipients of remittances within the territory of Northeast China, if they move to Japan, or recipients of remittances in Guan Nei, when they move to Japan, may receive their remittances at the Japanese post office. The exchange rules are recorded below:

Exchange Rules: Chapter 1, General Rules: Article 1: The usual exchange between "Man" and China is the "Man" China exchange. Article 2: The post offices handling the "Man" China exchange have separate announcements. Article 3: The exchange amount remitted or transferred to the same person on the same day, mainly based on postal services, is divided into three types: 100 yuan limit, 400 yuan limit, and 800 yuan limit. Article 5: The exchange fee for each copy is as follows: up to 10 yuan, 15 cents; up to 20 yuan, 25 cents; up to 30 yuan, 35 cents; up to 50 yuan, 55 cents; up to 100 yuan, 1 yuan; up to 150 yuan, 1 yuan and 50 cents; above, every 50 yuan or odd number, an additional 50 cents will be added. (The next five chapters are omitted because they are the same as the main points of handling)

Main Points of Handling: The main points of handling exchange inside and outside the Guan have also been announced by the pseudo-Ministry of Transportation as follows: (1) Exchange Currency: The remittance from "Manchukuo" is based on the national currency, and the payment is made by the post office of the Republic of China in accordance with the conversion of its own currency. The remittances from the Republic of China are based on the national currency of the Republic of China, and the payment is made by the post office of "Manchukuo" after converting the national currency according to the market price at the time. (2) Maximum Exchange Limit: The exchange quota per person per day for remitting and returning to the post office is divided into three types. The exchange amount limits are as follows: Type A is up to 100 yuan, Type B is up to 400 yuan, and Type C is up to 800 yuan. (3) Exchange Rate: The exchange rate is exchanged in the local currency circulating in the remittance area in the Republic of China. When exchanging, a small amount of water money is charged. (4) Exchange Date: The exchange is made within six months from the date of issue of the bill of exchange. If there is no request, the remittance will still be returned to the remitting country. (5) Return Period: The remitting bureau notifies the remitter of the bill of exchange returned to the remitting country. The remitter, within one year from the date of issue of the bill of exchange, if he does not request the return of the remittance, the remittance will not be paid after the approval of the Minister of Transportation. (6) Exchange Statute of Limitations: The exchange is exchanged within three years from the date of issue of the bill of exchange. If the payment is not requested, it will be confiscated into the ""National Treasury." (7) Re-issuance: If the bill of exchange is lost, damaged, or contaminated, the remitter or recipient must request a certificate of re-payment from the remitting post office or the paying post office. At this time, if one jiao (stamp) is attached to the request, the Ministry of Posts and Communications of the original remitting country will re-issue a certificate and send it to the applicant. (8) Transfer When remitting from Japan, if the recipient of the Man-Japan exchange moves to the Republic of China, or if the recipient of the exchange remitted from Manchuria moves from the Republic of China to Japan, the remittance may be requested to be transferred. The water fee at this time will be deducted from the remittance and transferred by a new exchange. (15th)

Yu Bei Huojia County

Bumper Harvest of American Cotton

Yields Seven to Eight Times Greater Than Other Grains

Xinxiang Telegraph. In the past, rural Huojia County in Yu Bei relied heavily on the cultivation of indigo (a blue dye) as its main source of income. However, in recent years, the market has been flooded with foreign dyes, leading to the disappearance of local indigo altogether. Farmers were forced to switch to growing cotton. The cotton-producing areas include more than 160 villages such as Kangyi in the south, Zhonghe Town, Xiao Cheng, Da Guan, Xiaoguanzhuang, Wufu Village, Wanggaolou, and Luoqiying. When cotton cultivation first began, only 70 to 80 mu of cotton were planted per 100 mu of land. Moreover, due to the poor quality of the seeds, the plants were weak. Each cotton plant grew to a maximum height of only three feet, and the thickest branches were no thicker than a finger. As a result, each plant bore only 30 to 60 cotton bolls. This year, the villages switched to growing American cotton. The seeds were excellent, and the rainfall was favorable, resulting in vigorous growth. Each plant reached a height of six to seven feet, and the branches were mostly as thick as chicken eggs. Consequently, each plant produced as many as 200 to 300 cotton bolls. In the past, each mu yielded approximately 30 to 40 jin of cotton. This year, the average yield is expected to be 120 to 130 jin per mu. The current price of cotton is about 22 yuan per 100 jin (for seed cotton). This means a profit of 30 yuan per mu, which is seven to eight times more than growing autumn grains. The farmers are overjoyed with this unexpected harvest, which is truly a positive development in the effort to revitalize rural areas.

Anhui Province Relief Grain Levy Continues

Rice Merchants Voluntarily Stop Paying Relief Grain Tax on Exported Rice

Wuhu Correspondence. The Anhui Provincial Government, in order to provide relief for the drought in the province, established civil food regulation branches in Wuhu, Bengbu, and other places, and implemented a levy on exported rice at a rate of five sheng per shi. Merchants jointly opposed this measure. As a result, the relief grain collection point set up at Dashengguan on the Jiangsu border was abolished and moved to Xiliangshan in Anhui. Meanwhile, Anhui Chairman Liu Zhenhua telegraphed the Executive Yuan, requesting that it consider the special circumstances of southern Anhui and approve the continued collection for three months, ending at the end of March. The Executive Yuan decided to limit the collection to the end of December of last year and telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Government to comply. However, the Bengbu Chamber of Commerce noted that the relief grain collection point in that area had not yet complied with the order to cease collection and was still collecting as usual. They telegraphed the Wuhu Chamber of Commerce to inquire whether Wuhu was also continuing to collect. The Wuhu Chamber of Commerce replied that the collection point had not been abolished either. In addition to sending a telegram to the Bengbu Chamber of Commerce, they also planned to telegraph the central government and the Anhui Provincial Government, requesting that they issue a prompt order to abolish all relief grain collection points in various locations in order to reduce the burden and maintain commerce. The Wuhu Rice and Grain Transportation Guild, considering the matter to be closely related to their own interests, sent a letter to the Yanguan Customs Office on the 11th, stating that since the Executive Yuan had decided to abolish the relief grain tax, they would no longer pay it on exported rice and that there should be no such item as a relief grain tax in the future. They requested that the Customs Office inspect and release any rice merchants reporting rice for export. They also telegraphed the Anhui Provincial Government, explaining the reasons for not paying the relief grain tax and requesting a reply (11th).

Foreigner on British Ship Longhe

Beats Chinese Laborer, Leading to Suicide

Body Transported to Wuhu, Examination Reveals Serious Injuries

Shanghai and Wuhu Seamen Express Outrage and Offer Support

Wuhu Correspondence. The Longhe, a ship operated by the British firm Jardine Matheson & Co. on the Yangtze River, arrived in Wuhu on the 23rd of last month and unloaded the body of a Chinese laborer, Tong Tianhou, onto Jardine Matheson's pontoon. Upon learning that Tong had been brutally beaten by a ticket seller named Newman and forced to jump into the river, resulting in his death, the workers in the midships of all the Shanghai riverboat companies and the Wuhu Seamen's Union were filled with indignation. They formed a support association to investigate and engage in serious negotiations. The Shanghai Chinese Seamen's Union believed that the matter not only involved the mistreatment of Chinese laborers but also the disregard for the lives of Chinese people. It instructed the Wuhu Seamen's Union to investigate the details. The Wuhu Union sent representatives to the Public Security Bureau's water patrol and the local court to investigate the matter in detail. The truth of the matter is as follows:

Tong Tianhou, a worker in the midships of the Xianghe, also owned by Jardine Matheson, had missed the Xianghe's earlier departure from Shanghai to Hankou. Fearing that this would affect his job, he hastily took a Shanghai-Nanjing train to Nanjing. However, by the time he arrived at Xiaguan, the Xianghe had already passed Nanjing and sailed upstream. He then boarded the Longhe, intending to catch up with the Xianghe at the upstream docks. When the Longhe reached the Jiangning County section of the river, the foreign ticket seller, Newman, discovered that Tong had not purchased a ticket and was not wearing his certificate badge. He demanded that Tong buy a ticket. Tong explained that he was a worker on a sister ship and that he had left his badge on the Xianghe because he was not on duty. He also explained that he did not have much money and repeatedly requested to buy a half-price ticket. However, the foreigner not only refused but also punched and kicked him repeatedly. He insisted that Tong buy a full-price ticket. Tong was powerless against the abuse and did not have enough money to buy a full-price ticket. Although the ship was large, he had nowhere to stand. In desperation, he saw no other option than to leave the ship. He jumped into the river immediately. Passengers on the ship, unable to bear the sight, protested to the captain. The captain stopped the ship and had Tong pulled out of the water. However, he was barely breathing and on the verge of death. When the Longhe arrived at Yanhu and docked at the pontoon, Tong had already died. The captain ordered the workers to carry Tong's body ashore, and the person in charge of the pontoon reported the matter to the local court. After examination by Prosecutor Wang Gai, accompanied by clerks and police officers, it was determined that Tong Tianhou had three serious injuries to the back of his head and arms, which were the fatal wounds. The deceased was from Hubei and was about 30 years old. He had worked on the Xianghe for many years. The Wuhu Seamen's Union has reported the above facts to the Shanghai General Union and has planned steps to engage in serious negotiations with Jardine Matheson & Co. to seek justice for the deceased and protect human rights (13th).

Lu Xi Refugees Flock to Jinan

Numbering About Four to Five Thousand People

The Municipal Government is Planning Relief Efforts

Jinan Correspondence. Last year, counties such as Puyang, Fanxian, Shouyang, and Yanggu in western Shandong suffered from floods again. During this harsh winter, refugees have been flocking to Jinan in search of food. Several thousand refugees have built shacks and settled in the flooded areas west of Guanzhaying and south of the Jinpu Railway's Xiawa. During the day, men try to find manual labor but are unsuccessful. Elderly, weak women beg in the mud, unable to get enough to eat. At night, they return to their shacks and sleep on wet mats. When these impoverished refugees first arrived in Jinan, the municipal government built earthen houses east of Gangzi and south of the Jiaoji Railway to house them, creating a village-like community with police guarding it, which was quite orderly. Now, a special request has been submitted to the municipal government to handle this situation in the same way as before. According to this request, the municipal government dispatched personnel to investigate and found that there were approximately 1,500 shacks built by refugees west of Guanzhaying, with each shack housing between three and five refugees, totaling approximately four to five thousand people. Adult men drag small carts in the Tianqiao area, but their daily wages are barely enough to afford one full meal. The elderly, weak, and women have no other way to make a living except by begging. Beggars are appearing in the streets in large numbers. Although the police have tried to stop them, they cannot be completely prevented from begging in small alleys due to their desperate need for food. These refugees are suffering from hunger and cold, and their situation is already pitiful. Moreover, their shacks are located in low-lying areas, and if it rains or snows, they will be trapped in water and snow, making it even more difficult to survive. Mayor Wen Chenglie previously requested the establishment of winter shelters and was authorized to establish three, each limited to 500 people. However, recent investigations have revealed that each shelter is housing more than 600 or 700 people. The number of indigent people in the city's poorhouse has also increased sharply to more than 900. There is no way to free up funds, and the housing is insufficient. According to the proposal submitted by Zhou, erecting temporary shelters to provide shelter would cost approximately 2,000 yuan, which is also a significant amount. The city is finding it difficult to raise these funds. A request has been submitted to the provincial relief committee for relief grain or to find housing, and the Red Swastika Society has sent people to investigate and distribute flour to provide relief.

Detailed Report from the Magistrate of Caoxian County

The Beginning and End of the Sun Lawsuit

The Sun Family Has a Wife and Children

So-called Hardship Love Like This

Jinan Correspondence. The case of Sun Defu and Han Guiqing, known as "Seeking a Husband Thousands of Miles Away" and "Hardship Love," was widely circulated for a time. Yesterday, according to a report from Wei Hanzhang, the magistrate of Caoxian County, to the Department of Civil Affairs, the lawsuit of Sun was described in detail, stating that Sun had other intentions and that Sun had a wife and children at home. The people who praised Sun and Han also feel disappointed. The original report is disclosed below: "On January 4, 1935, the Jinan Evening News published a detailed report on the interview with Han Guiqing, a lady who sought her husband Sun Defu thousands of miles away. And on December 29, 1934, the Dagong Bao published a report on Sun Defu and his wife, who fought against difficulties and took revenge for their father. The reports that Sun Defu's father was murdered by Li Baoqing and seized his property do not conform to the facts. Sun Defu was originally from Kaocheng County, Henan Province. He had a wife, Sun Qu, who was 33 years old, and a 7-year-old son and a 3-year-old daughter. There is a written report from Sun Defu himself to prove it. The Dagong Bao reported that Chairman Han personally reviewed and ordered Li Baoqing and others to repay Sun Defu 60,000 yuan and 5 qing of land, which is not true. Based on the above, it is enough to prove that the reports are all false and fabricated facts with other intentions. I will carefully describe the detailed facts of this case to your seat. On May 6, 1933, I received a telegram from Commander-in-Chief Han Yu, stating that Sun Defu accused Li Baoqing of seizing property. I was ordered to send Li Baoqing to the province for trial within half a month. The county magistrate personally led officers and soldiers to arrest Li Baoqing and sent him to the province for trial. Later, I received a letter from the Military Law Office of the Third Route Command of the Expeditionary Army, stating that the case of Sun Defu accusing Li Baoqing was inconsistent with the facts and could not be judged. Now, I received an order from the commander to send the plaintiff and defendant back to the original county for detailed investigation. I was ordered to handle the case accordingly and report the handling situation. I was also asked to send 15 contracts, 2 receipts, and 1 volume. I repeatedly investigated the case. Sun Defu confessed that he was from Sunjia Village, Chumaodian, Kaocheng County, Henan Province. Because of his old grudges with Li Baoqing's family, his father was murdered by Li Gaojian and others instigated by Li Baoqing in the 34th year of Guangxu. Li Gaojian also led people to rob his wife and children for ransom. Li Gaojian also led dozens of people to find him and try to murder him several times without success. In 1929, he filed a lawsuit in the Henan Provincial Government. Chairman Han ruled that he was given 2 qing of land and a house. Because he did not pay the grain tax, he could not manage the property. Later, he filed two lawsuits. After mediation, Li Baoqing gave him 3 items and 48 mu of land, and 46 tile houses. He had a written contract, but he refused to comply. Li Baoqing confessed that he was 36 years old. Sun Defu's father died during the Guangxu period. At that time, he was only 10 years old. He did not have the ability to instigate murder. Li Gaojian was three or four years older than him and was also the head of the family. Not only could he not be used by him, but a person of a few years old had no courage to kill. His complaint was false. The people can testify

Transactions, almost stopped. As a result, the bank was greatly affected. Few people asked about the sale of real estate. Moreover, because the end of the year was approaching, the city's financial resources were tight, and depositors withdrew their money one after another. The bank's current money had already been used for real estate investment and could not be paid in time, which led to a bank run. At first, the bank planned to borrow 500,000 yuan from a bank in Hong Kong to meet the urgent needs, using the bank's assets as collateral. However, the mortgage of the assets required legal procedures such as newspaper registration, which delayed the time. Also, because one or two of the bank's directors were irresponsible, the loan failed to materialize. The depositors' withdrawals increased day by day, and the bank was helpless. On the 4th of this month, it announced its closure. At the same time, the head office on Des Voeux Road, Hong Kong, also went bankrupt. The Shanghai branch followed suit. On the evening of the 5th, the Hong Kong head office convened a board meeting to discuss the aftermath. It was decided to issue a formal notice to convene a meeting of shareholders and creditors on the 16th of this month to discuss the investment of assets and the maintenance of the interests of depositors. In Guangzhou, the bank's creditors, who had been greatly in debt, immediately established a creditors' association registration office and hired lawyers to handle everything (9th).

Ministry of Industry and Commerce Reorganizes Fishermen's Associations

Consulting Various Provincial and Municipal Governments for Implementation

Beijing Dispatch. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce believes that the purpose of establishing fishermen's associations is to increase the knowledge and skills of fishermen, improve their lives, and develop production. In areas with thriving fisheries that have not yet established fishermen's associations, they should be urged to organize them as soon as possible. In areas that already have fishermen's associations but whose organizations are unsound, or where disputes arise frequently and no achievements can be made, they should be guided and reorganized in accordance with the law to fulfill the central government's earnest intention to improve fisheries. Therefore, eight items for attention by the competent supervisory authorities of fishermen's associations have been formulated and sent to the provincial and municipal governments along the Yangtze River and the coast, and the Weihaiwei Management Office has been ordered to transmit them to its subordinates for compliance. The items for attention by the competent supervisory authorities of fishermen's associations are as follows: "(1) In counties, cities, or important ports that meet the requirements of Articles 4, 1, and 2 of the Fishermen's Association Law but have not established fishermen's associations, they should be urged to organize them in accordance with the law. (2) Fishermen or those engaged in the production, transportation, storage, and management of aquatic products who initiate the organization of fishermen's associations in accordance with the law and have been approved for registration by the competent supervisory authorities should be ordered to submit the date of establishment, the resumes of elected officers, and the membership list to the department for record. (3) When the terms of directors and supervisors of fishermen's associations reach the prescribed limit, they should be urged to hold elections in accordance with the law and report them to the department for record. (4) Fishermen's associations that have been approved for record should be urged to actively carry out their prescribed tasks and local fishery conditions. (5) When fishermen's associations decide to raise business funds and carry out joint ventures, they should submit a business plan and a budget to the competent supervisory authorities for approval before collecting funds. (6) Fishermen's associations that have been established for more than one year should be urged to report to the department for record each year in accordance with the provisions of Article 17 of the Fishermen's Association Law. (7) Fishermen's associations that do not work hard in accordance with the tasks prescribed by their respective associations should report the facts to the higher authorities for handling at any time. (8) In areas with thriving fisheries that have not established fishermen's associations, existing fishery organizations established by fishermen should be urged to reorganize in accordance with the provisions of Article 28 of the Fishermen's Association Law within a time limit. If fishermen's associations have been established, these organizations should be ordered to merge into the fishermen's associations. If they do not merge, the organizations outside the fishermen's associations should be ordered to cease activities."

Menhai

Bandit Searches Wu Qingyu's Village

In Zhengzhi Township, Qidong Second District, the large household Wu Qingyu Village was suddenly raided by more than a dozen bandits with flashlights and guns late the other night. They broke into the village, twisted the arm of the village's accountant Xu Wentong, and forced him to hand over silver dollars. When he refused, they beat him with wooden sticks, causing him to be covered in injuries. They then went to the room, turned over boxes and cabinets, searched arbitrarily, and left after about an hour. After the incident, an inventory revealed a loss of more than one hundred silver dollars. However, Xu's injuries were very serious, and his life may be in danger.

Total Agency for Trafficking in Southeastern China Smashed

Recently, young women have been disappearing from this county and neighboring counties from time to time. The local public security authorities have ordered a serious investigation. Nanjing, Bengbu, etc. The Wuxi general agency entices and buys young women and transports them to Zhenjiang, Bengbu and other places for sale. Recently, there was news of opening a brothel in Zhenjiang. The Bengbu and Zhenjiang branch agencies sent letters to Wuxi to contact and buy women. Ma Zishan then dispatched his feathers and outcasts to lure and deceive them. Ma Zishan negotiated and informed the Zhenjiang branch agency to send Xu Kunlin, Li Peiyu and others to Wuxi to purchase them. Changshu

The County Government Joins Various Banks

To Establish a Joint Treasury

The Changshu County Government has been suffering from reduced tax revenue and severe financial constraints in recent years. It has joined forces with the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Bank of Jiangsu, and the Farmers Bank to form a joint treasury, which will be implemented starting on the 1st of next month. One of the four banks will be designated as the representative bank to manage the collection and distribution of funds evenly. The rate is 4,000 yuan. If the amount is less than this, it will not be distributed for the time being. If it exceeds 4,000 yuan, the balance will be distributed in units of 100 yuan. The representative period is six months. Each bank will take turns to serve as the representative bank. The first representative will be the Bank of Jiangsu starting next month, followed by the Farmers Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. The end of each term will be at the end of June and the end of December. From now on, the four banks will equally bear the burden of the county's tax collection period and various financial loans. Other companies that wish to participate may join at any time.

The Deepest Freeze of the Great Cold Season Only Arrived Yesterday; Lowest Temperature Was 24.8 Degrees

Since the heavy fog on the 10th of this month, followed by a rainstorm on the 14th, accompanied by sleet, as the saying goes, "Seeing snow brings clear skies," the weather suddenly turned cold and clear on the 15th. In recent days, the north wind has been howling, indicating severely cold weather. With the Great Cold solar term arriving on the 21st, the temperature has been gradually decreasing. The lowest temperature on the 13th was 50.2 degrees. Due to the drastic change in weather on the 14th, there was no record, and on the 15th, it was only 30 degrees. According to the Observatory's report yesterday, the lowest temperature was 24.8 degrees, and the highest was only 37 degrees. With a difference of over 20 degrees in three days, ice was seen in the city's ditches yesterday morning, and it had not completely melted by noon. Even tap water froze in some places.

Jianghai Customs Notice; Measures to Prohibit Carrying National Currency

Limited to 1,000 Yuan Per Person Within the Country; Passengers and Crew Going Abroad Are Not Allowed to Carry Any

Tang Haian, Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, and Luo Fude, Tax Commissioner, acting upon orders, have issued Notices No. 1408 and No. 1413 regarding the prohibition of passengers and crew from carrying national currency. Now, further orders have been received from the Ministry of Finance, stipulating three measures as follows: (1) Passengers carrying silver dollars to various parts of the country are still limited to 1,000 yuan per person as before. (2) Passengers and crew going abroad, or those passing through foreign ports en route to another domestic port, are not allowed to carry any national currency. (3) Passengers and crew traveling to areas where silver standard currency is not in use are strictly prohibited from carrying national currency. All merchants and people are hereby notified.

Five Exchanges in the City Vigorously Advocate for Exchange Tax and Jointly Appeal to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for Assistance; Mu Ouchu Reported on Tax Collection by the Ministry of Finance; Brokers' Associations Held General Meetings Separately Yesterday

The Council of the five exchanges of the city--gold, securities, flour and miscellaneous grains--and the five brokers' associations, specially hosted a banquet for the members of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at the Atlantic Restaurant yesterday at 7 p.m. regarding the central government's imposition of exchange tax. They appealed for assistance. The details are recorded as follows.

Participating Representatives:

Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Jin Runxiang, Standing Committee Member, Mu Ouchu, Chairman of the Gauze Association, Zhang Weiru from the Securities Association, Xu Busun from the Gold Association, Wang Yiting from the Flour Association, Gu Xinyi from the Miscellaneous Grains Association, and representatives from the brokers' associations: Wang Zhengru, Wu Limen, Zhu Anfu, Qiu Liangui, He Peiyuan from Securities; Zhan Liansheng, Wang Yingchang, Wang Jiafu, Gao Qiumei, Zhang Zhusun from Gold; Zhang Weiyun, Zhu Jiansheng, Xia Rongchang, Wang Zhongliang, Yang Jingcheng from Flour; Chuan Changyu, Xue Chengzhang, Xu Jianqi, Qu Guanfu, Ding Futing from Miscellaneous Grains; and Bian Futang, Wu Xunqing, Shao Wenmei, Zhang Bojin, Kuang Jian from Gauze, etc., more than 40 people attended.

Chairman's Report: Mu Ouchu was elected chairman. He stood up and reported, saying: "In recent years, the world has been affected by the economic depression, and domestically, we have been plagued by floods, droughts, bandits, and disasters, resulting in rural bankruptcy, industrial and commercial decline, and stagnation of the circulation of goods and wealth. The national economy is deteriorating, and the future crisis is terrifying. The exchange is the balancing mechanism of the modern economic organization. The sale and purchase of goods are based on fairness. Although there are commission earnings, the responsibilities are also very important. Now the Ministry of Finance is imposing exchange tax to increase the national treasury income. When the news came, the business of each exchange greatly reduced. In the future, after the review and approval of the Legislative Yuan and the implementation of the tax, it will not only increase the burden of the buyers and sellers of the exchanges, but also fundamentally affect the position of the exchanges. Each exchange has sent representatives to the central government to petition, and the result is that they will be allowed to attend the review meetings of the Finance and Economic Committees of the Legislative Yuan to make statements. It is now heard that the tax rate will soon be submitted for review. Therefore, it is decided to appeal to the central government to temporarily postpone the matter. This is not only for the benefit of the exchanges themselves, but also to reduce the burden on industry and commerce. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce is the leading organization of all industries, and the hardships of merchants can be seen without any reservations. We hope that Chairman Yu will make a fair proposition and do his best to assist." Then Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Wen Lanting, Wu Limen and others expressed their opinions. The banquet ended at 8:30.

Representatives to Nanjing:

The exchange authorities have decided to appoint Xu Busun, Mu Ouchu, Gu Xinyi, Zhang Weiru, and Wang Yiting as the five directors to be representatives to Nanjing. The brokers' associations have already appointed Wang Zhengru, Zhan Liansheng, Zhang Weiyun, Chuan Changyu, and Bian Futang as the five representatives to request to attend the meeting. According to Mu Ouchu, chairman of the Gauze Exchange, the 18th of this month is the first plenary meeting of the Legislative Yuan. The news from Beijing tonight said that the tax will be discussed at the meeting, which may not be true. The exchange tax has been submitted to the Finance and Economic Committees and has not been formally reviewed. According to the meeting procedure, it has not yet been submitted to the meeting for discussion. The representatives of each exchange are now waiting for the notification from the Legislative Yuan to Shanghai. After the date is determined, they will go to Nanjing.

Brokers' Association:

The general meetings of the five exchanges, including gold, securities, gauze, flour, and miscellaneous grains, were originally scheduled to be held separately at each exchange on the night before last. In addition to the Gauze Brokers' Association notifying the convening of the meeting to discuss the various methods, the four secretaries of the Gold, Securities, Flour, and Miscellaneous Grains Exchanges met at 3 pm yesterday. More than 40 people attended the Securities Association, chaired by Wang Zhengru. More than 80 people attended the Gold Association, chaired by Zhan Liansheng. More than 30 people attended the Flour Association, chaired by Zhang Weiyun. More than 30 people attended the Miscellaneous Grains Association, chaired by Chuan Changyu. The resolutions of the general meeting of the five exchange brokers' associations are as follows: (1) The five exchanges take unified action to achieve the goal of exempting the exchange tax. (2) If the central government ignores the difficulties of merchants and implements the tax on schedule, all will sacrifice business. (3) Appoint representatives to Nanjing to attend the review meeting of the Legislative Yuan to strive for it.

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Tunan" ship was sailing from Tianjin back to Shanghai on July 10, 1933. When it sailed to Chengshanjiao, Shandong, it was sunk by the Japanese shipping company Dalian Steamship Company's "Changchun Maru." Reactions to Merchants' Request to Stop Cotton Futures Trading; The China Cotton Industry Federation Submits a Document to the Government

The China Cotton Industry Federation submitted a document to the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Ministry of Industry, and the Municipal Government regarding the fact that a few manufacturers have requested the cessation of cotton futures trading on the China Merchants Yarn and Cloth Exchange due to the high price of cotton and the low price of yarn. The document states that cotton futures trading has nothing to do with the high price of cotton and the low price of yarn, and requests that the original business be maintained. It is learned that recently a few manufacturers have requested the cessation of cotton futures trading on the China Merchants Yarn and Cloth Exchange due to the high price of cotton and the low price of yarn in an attempt to remedy the situation. Merchants and others in the cotton industry dare not agree. All countries in the world have measures to equalize the prices of agricultural products and help rural villages and farmers, but there are no measures to suppress the prices of agricultural products and help factories. In 1934, comparing cotton prices around the world, our country was the lowest, and Shanghai was the lowest in our country. The reason why we achieved this result is that we rely on the agencies to set standard prices every day and equalize market prices according to law, so yarn factories are not easy to oppress cotton merchants and farmers. However, the various yarn factories of the China Merchants side take the high price of cotton and the low price of yarn as the only reason for the loss. They do not ask themselves how their technology is, how their management is. If they are not improved, even if the raw materials are extremely low, the yarn factories will still have no way. The evidence is that some Chinese and foreign yarn factories also have surpluses last year. Therefore, the high price of cotton and the low price of yarn cannot be used as an excuse. Moreover, between the summer and autumn of last year, some Chinese yarn factories expected a bumper harvest and the price of cotton would fall, so they sold a large amount of cotton yarn without buying cotton. When the new cotton was on the market, foreign yarn factories rushed to buy it, while the Chinese yarn factories still waited for the price to fall. By now, they have purchased domestic cotton at high prices, and because of the silver problem, the price difference between foreign cotton and domestic cotton is even greater. Therefore, it is secretly said that the high price of cotton is caused by the manufacturers themselves. What is there to complain about? In the past, the price of cotton was only determined by the manufacturers. It is not the case now. The height of the cotton price is fundamentally driven by the farmers. In recent years, our government has spared no effort to revive the countryside. The financial sector's rural lending has directly benefited the countryside. As farmers, they will definitely wait for the price to sell. The high price of cotton is a major reason. Manufacturers are also part of the people, so why must they suppress it to make it low? Or, the price of buying and selling still listens to the manufacturers. It is self-sufficient. Merchants and others have been in the cotton industry for a long time. They usually purchase cotton from all over the country and concentrate it in Shanghai. Because of inconvenient transportation, goods cannot arrive in Shanghai on time, and prices fluctuate again. The purchase and sale of sets have been no different. If cotton is stopped from being auctioned, cotton merchants and farmers will both be harmed. This kind of proposition cannot be adopted. It is reasonable to list the facts and request verification. The cotton futures trading rate should be maintained according to the old regulations to ensure the safety of farmers and merchants.

It has been formally approved by the company's board of directors. Mr. Yang is a native of Wuxian, Jiangsu. He is 51 years old, studied at St. John's College, graduated from Nanyang Public School, studied in Belgium and France in Europe, and has a master's degree in commerce from Anderwo University in Belgium. He served as secretary of the Belgian Legation for half a year and was transferred to be a member of the Finance Inspection Group. From 1916 to 1921, he served as general manager of Huiye Bank and general manager of Xinheng Bank. He successively served as a member of the Political Committee, the Economic Committee, and the Finance Committee, and as a specialist member of the Customs Tariff Conference. From 1928 to 1933, he was the manager of the Bank of Communications and was in charge of all the banks under the Ministry of Communications. He served as a senior advisor and chief auditor of the Bank of Communications and is currently a director and advisor of the Bank of Communications.

Yangzhou

Bandits Kill and Rob in Qilidian

At No. 13 Douji Lane in the city, there were two Hu brothers: the elder, Chuanjue, 24 years old, who worked as a teacher at the Meihan Middle School in the city; and the younger, Chuanhong, who worked as a teacher at the Yangzi Elementary School in the Twelve Forts area of the county. Both were married. Their father had passed away early, but their mother was still alive. The family was of modest means. Recently, their father's grave site was encroached upon. The two brothers went to Qilidian cemetery outside the West Gate this morning (the 15th) to investigate. Unexpectedly, when they passed Sun Family Village, two plainclothes bandits suddenly appeared, both armed with handguns, and ordered them to stop, robbing them on the spot. Chuanhong resisted the bandits and was shot in the left side, falling to the ground in great pain and dying instantly. Chuanjue, seeing the scene, was terrified and stood frozen by the roadside. The two bandits, fearing that there would be many passersby since it was daytime, fled immediately. Afterwards, the grave keeper, surnamed Chen, arrived after hearing the noise and brought the frightened Chuanjue to his house. He sent someone into the city to report to the family and dispatched people out of the city to carry the deceased Chuanhong to the Great Fortune God Temple. Chuanjue was carried into the city to seek medical treatment. It is reported that the family is preparing to report to the county government and the court for an autopsy and to apprehend the murderers.

Municipal Public Security Bureau

Construction of Police Cemetery Begins

Former Director Wen Hong'en Will Be Buried There

The Municipal Public Security Bureau, out of concern for the city's police officers who sacrificed themselves for the country, society, or died from illness due to hard work, and in view of the fact that they had no fixed burial place after death, specially purchased a piece of land in Jiangwan to build the Shanghai Municipal Police Cemetery, so that police officers who died in the line of duty could have a resting place after death. Nisshin Kisen Kaisha

Unable to Resume Business in China

Only Ten Ships Sailing on the Yangtze and Northern Seas

At its peak, the Japanese-owned Nisshin Kisen Kaisha had over 20 ships sailing on the upper, middle, and lower reaches of the Yangtze River and on the northern and southern sea routes. Since the Northeast Incident and the Shanghai War, business has been severely hit. Despite repeated attempts to recover, it has ultimately failed. To date, the Shanghai-Hankou line still has the Fengyang, Xiangyang, Luoyang, and Nanyang, totaling four ships. The Northern and Southern Seas routes have the Huashan, Songshan, Lushan, and Tangshan, totaling four ships. There is one ship each on the Hankou-Yichang and Yichang-Chongqing lines. The total number of ships is ten. Each voyage, apart from transshipment of goods from Japan, has very few Chinese merchants. Passenger fare income is only enough to cover the ship's expenses. Therefore, it is currently only maintaining existing routes, waiting for an opportunity.

Chamber of Commerce Writes to Customs Regarding

Anchorage for Pig Boats on the Huangpu River

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce wrote to the Jianghai Customs Superintendent yesterday, stating, "We are writing regarding a letter received from the Fresh Pig Industry Association this month, which states that the Jiangbei Six Port Pig Boat Workers United Office has written that our pig boats have been transporting fresh pigs from various ports in Jiangbei to Shanghai for decades, unloading them in front of the Xuejiabang Oil Mill Wharf in Nanshi. Unexpectedly, recently, when ships anchored at Xuejiabang, they were unjustifiably fined by the water patrol team, occurring several times a day. After investigation, most pig boats anchor at Xuejiabang within the Jianghai Customs buoys, without obstructing the waterway, while other types of ships, such as timber and miscellaneous grain, have fixed anchorages. Only our pig boats anchor in open spaces, leading to arrests and fines. Our boatmen's families depend on transporting goods for a small fee to make a living. If we do not request assistance to negotiate for a proper anchorage, what will become of our industry? Therefore, we urgently request a joint effort, otherwise our boatmen will have to unload at Wusong and no longer sail to Shanghai. It is also claimed that there are three sand boat buoys in the Huangpu River in front of Xuejiabang, with large sand boats and fishing boats anchored in the middle. Pig boats must detour to unload, which is dangerous in high tide and with favorable winds. We urge your association to find a way to resolve the difficulty to facilitate navigation. According to this, our industry has leased a shoreline from the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau in Nanshi at Xuejiabang, paying an annual shoreline usage fee, and has built a wharf to unload pigs for many years. Having been approved to build a wharf, there must be a corresponding anchorage; otherwise, the wharf would be useless. However, various types of ships on the Huangpu River often take precedence over the owner, arbitrarily anchoring in front of our wharf, causing pig boats arriving in Shanghai to have no place to dock. If they accidentally anchor in an open space, they are accused of obstructing traffic and fined. It is not our pig boats that are to blame for this obstruction of traffic. Regarding the request to resolve the danger of navigation, we sent personnel to investigate and found that pig boats sailing to Xuejiabang in Nanshi to unload must detour to avoid sand boat buoys, which is indeed prone to danger. If a method could be devised to request that the two middle buoys be moved to the open space on the south side and connected to buoy number six, pig boats coming south from the north could sail directly to the front of the wharf, lower their anchors, and moor. It would be both convenient for navigation and beneficial for berthing, a win-win situation. A sketch map is attached. It is feared that pig boats have nowhere to anchor, and detours can easily create dangerous voyages. If pig boats hesitate, it will be a great concern for the future of our business. Therefore, we have no choice but to request your association's assistance in forwarding a letter to the Jianghai Customs to request (1) to designate an anchorage for pig boats at Xuejiabang in Nanshi as soon as possible, (2) to move the two middle sand boat buoys south and connect them to buoy number six to facilitate pig boat navigation and berthing. Your kindness will be greatly appreciated. Two attached maps are sent to the association. We find that the two points requested by the association are not only related to the safety of pig boat workers and the avoidance of unjust punishment but also greatly beneficial to water traffic administration, reducing the danger of navigation. The matter is urgent, and the request is very proper. Accordingly, we enclose the original attached map and send a letter to forward it. We ask your superintendent to forward it to the Customs for approval and implementation, so as to benefit industry and commerce. This is our public obligation."

Zhang Zhongyu's Family

Kidnapped Child Escapes Danger

Three Kidnappers Arrested

Sent to Court This Morning

Zhang Zhongyu, a wealthy silk merchant, has been operating the Pinghe and Siyi silk factories in Huaxing Lane on Baoding Road and Qingfuli on Zhoujiazui Road. His business has prospered, and he has accumulated some savings, attracting the attention of bandits. On December 12 of last year, at around 10:00 a.m., several kidnappers, using the pretext of distributing red eggs, entered Zhang's residence at No. 10 Senchangli, Kunming Road, by tricking them into opening the door. They rushed in, threatening with guns, and kidnapped Zhang's four-year-old son, Yangge, and fled. Zhang reported the incident to the police, who issued an arrest warrant. However, Zhang suddenly received a letter from the bandits some days ago, demanding a huge ransom, and scheduled a meeting at Room 321 of the Far East Hotel on Tibet Road at 11:00 a.m. yesterday. The case was discovered by Chief Inspector Lu Liankui of the General Investigation Department of the General Police Department, who directed detectives Liu Shaokui, Feng Zhiming, and Song Bingzheng to secretly go to Room 321 of the Far East Hotel at around 10:00 a.m. and arrest three kidnappers, including Zhu Huawen. They learned the location of the kidnapped child and rushed to the kitchen of No. 9 Guangxingli, Wuchang Road, and rescued the child, Zhang Yangge, from danger. A woman surnamed Wei Wang, who was watching the child, was also arrested and taken to the police station. After escorting Zhang Yangge home and handing him over to his father, the police are now strictly interrogating the suspects to apprehend their accomplices. The arrested suspects will be sent to the First Special District Court's Criminal Division for investigation this morning.

Zhongfu Bank

Grand Theft Case Adjudicated

Sun Ruifu Married with Stolen Money

Therefore Gold Ornaments Must Also Be Recovered

Hu Honglai and Others Sentenced

During the Mid-Autumn Festival holiday of the lunar calendar this year, the Zhongfu Bank on Renji Road was burglarized, and 21,000 yuan in paper money was stolen. After the bank discovered the theft, it reported it to the police and requested an investigation. Later, Chief Inspector Lu Liankui and Detective Liu Shaokui of the General Investigation Department arrested Wang Xiaohua, the main offender in the case, and handed him over to the First Special District Court, which sentenced him to one year and six months in prison. Subsequently, Chief Inspector Lu discovered that the mastermind of the case was Hu Honglai, a coppersmith from Anhui at the Zhongfu Bank, who had stolen the keys and committed the crime. After the case, Hu fled to Zhenjiang. Detective Chen Chenggui and Wu Hanzhang were dispatched to the Dahua Hotel in Zhenjiang, and arrested Hu and his accomplices, Sun Ruifu and Shi Haiquan, and brought them back to Shanghai for investigation and detention by the First Special District Court. This has been reported in detail in this newspaper. Now, after investigation by the detectives, the stolen money borrowed by Hu et al. and the jewelry purchased with the stolen money have been successively recovered, totaling approximately 3,306 yuan in cash and jewelry. However, Sun Ruifu, after receiving his share of the stolen goods, used 300 yuan in cash and 1,100 yuan in jewelry to betroth Fang Linxiang (23 years old), daughter of Fang Meichun, who lived at No. 15 Derunfang, Er'erjin Road. When the police went to the Fang's house to retrieve the jewelry and cash, Fang refused. The police then requested the court to summon Fang Meichun to court. This morning, Judge Feng Shide continued the investigation in Criminal Division One. First, Fang Meichun and Fang Linxiang were summoned to the court. Under questioning, they admitted the facts but refused to return the gold jewelry, stating that if they had to return it, the marriage contract would have to be dissolved. The court stated that since it had been determined to be stolen goods, it should be returned. As for the marriage contract, it could be resolved separately according to law, and ordered the start of arguments. Attorney Yi Yaotang, representing the police, argued for severe punishment according to law. Judge Feng then announced the verdict in court, sentencing Hu Honglai to three years in prison, Sun Ruifu to two years and six months in prison, and Shi Haiquan to six months in prison as a warning.

Issue of China-Overseas Bank Returning Deposits

Still Awaiting Approval from the Head Office Shareholders Meeting

Since the China-Overseas Bank's Shanghai branch announced its closure due to the influence of the head office, it has requested lawyer Song Yunhui and accountant Wang Sifang to be appointed as liquidators to carry out the settlement of accounts and file for record, in preparation for receiving and paying everything. The statement of assets and liabilities has long been sent to Hong Kong by airmail, pending the resolution of the shareholders' meeting held in Hong Kong yesterday, and the record-filing procedures. The First Special District Court has also approved and recognized it as a Chinese legal entity, and in law, it can be liquidated separately from the Hong Kong head office, which is only registered with the British government. The funds of the branch deposited in other banks can no longer be denied and must be transferred to the liquidators so that they can be repaid immediately. According to lawyer Song, if the Hong Kong shareholders' meeting can approve it now, approximately 40% of the deposits can be paid out within days.

Shanghai County Anti-Opium Meeting

The Shanghai County Opium Prohibition Committee held its fourteenth meeting yesterday, chaired by Committee Chairman Pan. Excerpts from the agenda are as follows: (1) Regarding the joint petition from the Minhang Heji Opium Paste Shop and the Chunji Pinfen Smoking Shop to add two inspectors, with salaries subsidized by the merchants, there is no legal basis, and it is inconvenient to approve. If there is private trafficking or sales, it can be reported to the nearest Public Security Bureau at any time. (2) The position of director of the drug rehabilitation center, previously Dr. Yu was appointed as director on a trial basis. Now that the trial period has expired, a request will be made to the provincial authorities for formal appointment. (3) Dispatch personnel to verify opium addicts who have obtained licenses. Those who do not purchase and smoke from opium paste shops and smoking shops will be punished according to regulations. (4) Revised and approved the regulations on phased medical treatment as ordered. (5) Transfer those who have quit opium in batches to the center for implementation and investigation. (6) Order the Public Security organs to send police to summon those who have been ordered to quit opium to undergo treatment. Those who evade or delay will be arrested and prosecuted as unlicensed private smokers.

Temporary Measures for Prohibiting the Transportation of Cattle

Cattle Merchants Without Receipts Cannot Board the Train

Instructions from the Ministry of Railways to Be Followed by Both Railways

The Ministry of Railways previously instructed both railways to investigate and respond on whether the "Temporary Regulations for Prohibiting the Transportation of Cattle" and their implementing rules implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Government would hinder the operations of the two railways. The Car Service Department investigated and found that there were no hindrances. However, the requirement to verify the "Cattle Inspection Fee Receipt" issued by the Jiangsu Department of Finance before loading caused issues, as sometimes the train had arrived at the station, and the cattle were urgently waiting to be loaded, but the receipt was delayed, making it impossible to issue freight bills. Merchants often thought that railway staff were deliberately making things difficult, leading to misunderstandings. The Railway Bureau forwarded a request for a solution, and the Ministry has now forwarded a reply from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, stating that cattle merchants without receipts cannot board the train. If it is private transportation, the cattle merchant should be responsible. If the inspection has been completed but the receipt has not been issued, the inspection agency should be responsible. It cannot be considered that the Railway Bureau is deliberately obstructing. The Bureau has instructed the Car Service Department to be informed.

Jin Cotton Charged at Fifth-Class Rate

The Railway Bureau received a telegram from the Ministry of Railways, stating that cotton is classified into three types: fine, ordinary, and coarse, according to the Ministry's regulations for freight charges, which have been instructed to be followed. Now, after investigating the prices of cotton from various producing areas in Jin, it is found that they are similar to the Ministry's standards for coarse cotton and should be included in the fifth-class freight charges to facilitate transportation and joint transportation. Now that the cotton-producing areas are expanding, if the freight charges have not been approved by the Ministry, the production area prices should be investigated and handled separately in accordance with the Ministry's regulations. In addition to telegramming Zhengtai and other railways, you should also follow these instructions. Minister Gu Mengyu, Yuanye Printing.

Two People Freezing to Death Behind the Coal Slag Road

Yesterday afternoon, at around 2:00 p.m., two unidentified male corpses were found frozen to death inside a shed behind the isolation hospital on Nanshi Station East Road (behind the coal slag road). One, about 30 years old, was wearing a blue cloth shirt and torn black cloth pants and was bald. The other, about 20 years old, was wearing a gray military uniform, an old felt hat, no pants, and was barefoot. The Station Road Police Station, in addition to reporting to the West Gate Branch Bureau, also notified the local Baojia for post-mortem examination. The charitable society prepared coffins for burial.

Li Junhuan

Founding of the Buddhist Studies Library and Public Reading Room

Layman Li Junhuan, for the sake of promoting Buddhism, donated funds to establish a Buddhist Studies Library and Public Reading Room. It officially opened on the 20th of this month at No. 92 Baocheng Road, Qiujiang Road, Zhabei. It has collected hundreds of Buddhist books, and is open to the public for reading from morning to night every day. It is also open on Sundays and holidays. It opens the door to exhorting goodness and paves the way for propagating the Dharma. It will not be difficult to revive the declining social customs, and the sinking hearts of the people can be saved. However, because of his personal sincerity in propagating the Dharma, his strength is weak. Based on the principle of accumulating sand into a tower, he has to implore elders from all directions and virtuous people from the four continents to donate scriptures to cultivate this special cause, so that all beings can bathe in the Dharma and ascend to the Land of Ultimate Bliss together. Then the merits and rewards will be inconceivable.

Dalian Maru

Japanese Man Commits Suicide by Jumping into the Sea

Working in Lingyuan, Rehe

Is it a Venereal Disease or a Mental Illness?

On the Dalian Maru, a steamship belonging to the Dalian Steamship Company in this port, which arrived in Shanghai from Dalian this time, a Japanese passenger committed suicide by jumping into the sea. The situation is recorded as follows:

Japanese Man Comes to Shanghai for Illness　　After the four northeastern provinces were occupied by the Japanese puppets, most of the telecommunications agencies were staffed by Japanese. Asakura Kazuo, a Japanese employee of the Lingyuan Telegraph Bureau in Rehe Province, was 26 years old. Because he was ill in the telegraph bureau and could not work, it was said that he was suffering from a venereal disease, but he claimed to have a mental illness. Recently, he asked for leave to go to Dalian, and then came to Shanghai from Dalian, intending to recuperate from his illness. Therefore, he took the Dalian Maru to Shanghai.

Suicide by Jumping into the Sea Midway, Report to the Consulate Upon Arrival in Shanghai

The Japanese man's cabin was a third-class cabin. When the ship arrived in Qingdao, it was confirmed that Asakura was still on the ship. On the 13th, when the Dalian Maru left Qingdao and set sail for Shanghai, there was heavy fog and the ship was sailing at sea. Due to his illness, the Japanese man sneaked out of the cabin and jumped into the sea in the dark of night to end his life. However, no one knew when he jumped into the sea. When the Dalian Maru arrived in Shanghai and docked at the Huangpu Wharf, the passengers disembarked. The person in charge knew that one passenger was missing. At first, they only knew that one passenger was missing from the ship. Later, after checking the passenger list, they realized that the missing person was a Japanese. Because he worked for the puppet country and was a civil servant, the ship notified the company, which reported to the consulate. The Shanghai consulate sent two inspectors to the ship to investigate and search the cabin where the Japanese man lived. They found a note left by him about jumping into the sea. Combined with the fact that the crew saw him in Qingdao, it was known that he committed suicide by jumping into the sea outside the port of Qingdao.

Countries Compete

Far East Kerosene Market

Japanese Puppet Monopoly Falls to British and Dutch

Our Country's Authorities Have Long Paid Attention

British, American, and Russian countries compete for the Far East kerosene market. Since the implementation of the Japanese puppet monopoly policy, another situation has been created. Yesterday, I visited someone in the kerosene industry to inquire about the recent situation. According to the following three points he mentioned, the general trend of the Far East kerosene market in 1935 is clear at a glance. (1) Regarding the puppet country's monopoly policy, all parties have paid close attention to it since its promulgation, and there are many competitors. As a result, it was won by British and Dutch companies. (2) Japan's estimated kerosene demand for this year is 1.15 million kiloliters, and the quantity has been distributed to domestic and foreign companies. However, in order to protect its domestic kerosene industry, the government controls all prices, and the companies it trades with must keep six months of sales volume of oil. In case of emergency, the government can buy it back at a price. (3) The Chinese market has been affected by the recession in recent years, which is very different from the past. Sales have fallen sharply. Kerosene merchants in China have held many meetings to find ways to save the crisis. Our country's authorities have long been aware that kerosene is a very important item, and have been paying attention to the competition of kerosene from various countries in the Far East market. It is said that they have contacted a certain company in our country.

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Recruiting Technicians

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau is now planning to recruit one technician to handle industrial administration, industrial guidance, and editorial statistics. Male applicants who have graduated from the mechanical or electrical engineering departments of universities at home and abroad and have the above experience are qualified. The monthly salary is more than 100 yuan. Applicants can submit a detailed resume from January 20 to 28, along with qualification certificates, a recent half-length photo of 2 inches, and the desired minimum monthly salary, by registered mail to the bureau. (The envelope must indicate the word "application"). After reviewing the qualifications, a letter will be sent to inform the applicant to come to the bureau for testing. After the trial period, if the applicant is competent, he will be officially appointed as a technician.

Fire at Great Western Road

At around 11:00 yesterday morning, a fire broke out in a bungalow at No. 44 Xinjie, Great Western Road, Caojiadu, Shanghai, due to careless cooking with a briquette stove, which caused a fire to accumulate wood and dense smoke filled the area, breaking through the roof. Fortunately, the Caojiadu branch reported to the nearby Caojiadu Fire Brigade, which rushed to the scene and tried its best to put out the fire. A total of two bungalows were burned. Director Wang sent police to the scene and detained Gong Zhangshi, the owner of the fire, for questioning.

The 55th inspection report on the issuance reserve of Zhejiang Xingye Bank stated that the issuance of Zhejiang Xingye Bank has always been completely separated from the business aspect, and the reserve is sufficient. On the 16th of this month, the accountant Yan Ouke inspected and calculated that the cash reserve was more than 60%, and the guarantee reserve was less than 40%. The total amount of exchange issuance was 9,094,773 yuan, and the total amount of reserve was 9,094,773 yuan. Among them, the bank's issuance amount was 4,300,4773 yuan, the reserve was 3,167,773 yuan in cash, and the guarantee was 1,137,000 yuan. The amount used by the same bank was 4,790,000 yuan, the reserve was 2,884,000 yuan in cash, and the guarantee was 1,900,600 yuan.

Ban

Cigarette Giveaways Not Extended to the End of April

The Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Industry Association sent a letter to its member manufacturers, saying: "Dear Sirs, Shen Xin's two newspapers on January 13 reported that 'Nanjing's ban on cigarette giveaways has been approved by the Ministry of Finance to be extended to the end of April.' A special telegram on the 12th is very different from the Ministry of Finance's approval. Our association's Chairman Shen and committee members personally inquired about the matter with the Tax Affairs Department to determine whether this news was true. After the inquiry, we received a letter from the Tax Affairs Department's Beijing office. We are copying the original text for your company's reference. Sincerely, Tobacco Company, including one copy of the original letter: 'Dear Sirs, your letter regarding the newspaper reports that various cigarette factories have again applied for an extension of the ban on giveaways in cigarette packs, which was approved on the 12th to be extended to the end of April, requesting an investigation and reply. I went to the Coinage Department to inquire, and they said that the department has not continued to handle this case. The newspaper reports may be a mistake for the end of February, etc. I am replying to you for your reference. Sincerely.'"

Cheng Yujie

Resigns as Chairman of the Chinese and Foreign Grocery Association

Cheng Yujie, the chairman of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Grocery Industry Association, has been in charge of the association's affairs for three years. Last year, he also served as a supervisor of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the chief supervisor of the Cosmetics Industry Association. Recently, it was heard that Mr. Cheng has been running around in society for many years, which has led to exhaustion. He specially sent a letter to the Chinese and Foreign Grocery Industry Association to resign. His original letter said: "Dear Sirs, I have been serving society for several years now. At first, I was in charge of the affairs of the Cosmetics Industry Association, and then I took care of the Chinese and Foreign Grocery Industry, which was as loose as sand. Without cohesion, it is impossible to strengthen oneself. Therefore, in the autumn of the 20th year of the Republic of China, I joined forces with my colleagues to initiate the organization of the association. During the preparatory period, I strictly investigated and sealed up inferior goods. After the association was established, such as fighting for business tax, donating to military needs, raising funds for aviation, proposing freight prices, formulating industry rules, and issuing monthly reports, I have always been sincere in my efforts. Fortunately, I have received the enthusiastic love of my colleagues and the joint efforts of the public. I have been able to avoid mistakes and can be satisfied. I have always dared not lag behind others in serving the public. In addition to the positions of chairman and supervisor, I have almost abandoned my personal career. In recent years, the market has been in decline, which has never happened before. If I do not focus on operating a production business and continue to work for others, I will lose sight of the other. I am terrified of the future. Therefore, I sincerely request to resign from the position of chairman and elect a replacement according to law, so as to benefit the association's affairs. I will still use my qualifications as a committee member to assist in any way I can. I am sending this letter to you, hoping you will understand. Sincerely, the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Grocery Industry Association."

Letter

Dear Sirs, According to Cheng Heng, the compradore of our association's Longhe Wheel, I read a news item in the Shanghai News section of the Shenbao on January 11 entitled "Middle Cabin Worker Humiliated and Commits Suicide." It contains the words "Compradore Westerner Newman" and "the Compradore." After investigation, the case was a dispute between the ticket buyer Westerner Newman and the worker. Special Report

Peng Xiangying

Lecture on the Relationship Between Citizens and Air Defense

The Sino-Western Broadcasting Station, the day before yesterday, broadcast a lecture by Mr. Peng Xiangying entitled "The Relationship Between Citizens and Air Defense." The arguments were quite detailed and insightful. The text of his speech is published below:

The term "air defense" has indeed attracted the close attention of many countries and many people in the world recently. However, the origin of this term is only a little over a decade old. Since the European War, when Germany, England, and France used airplanes against each other to participate in combat, attacking important locations in their enemy countries and destroying combat forces, using this as a means to subdue the enemy, this new term was born. The countries at war at the time suddenly suffered damage from aerial attacks from airplanes and felt that the current national defense equipment, without prior air defense equipment, was not qualified for combat. Therefore, all countries in the world are actively building air defense in order to protect national standing and territorial integrity. The people of all countries also deeply feel that the protection of life and property, in this era, cannot be hoped for without air defense equipment. Therefore, everyone is desperately assisting the government in engaging in air defense construction, and at the same time actively engaging in personal protective measures. Especially with the activity of this term, it has occupied a large place in people's minds, and at all times, due to this new stimulus, people are loudly shouting "Save us, save us!" Only "Air defense, air defense," is the effective method. This term, receiving such enthusiastic calls from people, has thus become particularly new and prosperous.

However, this emerging term has been extremely active in various countries around the world for the past ten years or so, but we in China have turned a blind eye to it. It was not until the "September 18th" and "January 28th" incidents occurred, when Japan used its new and superior airplanes to bomb our Jinzhou, bomb our Shanghai, and other places, especially in the airspace of Hongkou and Zhabei, carrying out massacres and burning countless of our houses, bombing and killing countless of our people, that this term, like countless sharp knives falling from the sky, gave us recognition, making us realize that airplane bombing is indeed something to be feared. Therefore, this newly emerging term "air defense," which had gone unnoticed in China for more than a decade, has gradually been appreciated by the general public, who recognize the necessity of paying attention to it.

However, there are still many people who believe that air defense equipment only needs airplanes and anti-aircraft guns to carry out aerial and anti-air defense, and that the responsibility for air defense should be entirely borne by the government and has nothing to do with the people. This misconception is entirely due to a lack of thorough understanding of the mission of the air force and the elements of air defense. We must know that the enemy's airplanes come from various heights and from all directions. No matter how complete our military air defense is equipped and how accurate the anti-aircraft gun firing is, it is not easy to drive all enemy airplanes away and shoot them down outside the city. At the same time, we still need our unarmed civilians to engage in passive defense in order to achieve the overall goal of air defense. For example, taking London at the end of the European War, which used twelve squadrons of air defense airplanes and four hundred anti-aircraft guns to defend its airspace as an example, can make us understand. At that time, although London had such great air defense equipment, 10% to 30% of enemy airplanes still took advantage of the gaps to invade London's airspace to achieve their bombing purposes. This is clear and irrefutable proof. Moreover, purchasing various anti-aircraft guns and fighter airplanes requires enormous expense. Given China's current economic situation, it will be difficult to purchase large quantities of air defense weapons in a short period of time. Therefore, in today's China, it is especially necessary to have comprehensive civilian air defense equipment, and it is even more necessary for the people to have automatic protective measures. Because civilian air defense can be organized completely, although it cannot directly confront enemy airplanes, it can indirectly avoid or reduce the damage suffered during enemy air raids. Because when enemy airplanes attack, the most terrifying things are the dropping of incendiary bombs and poison gas bombs. As for the power of explosive bombs, it is limited to the local area of the point of impact, and the harm it causes is limited. However, incendiary bombs or poison gas bombs are different. They can turn the essence of an entire city into ashes in an instant, and the lives of the entire city will immediately be buried in a poisonous tomb, creating a scene of scorched earth with nothing left. As for the harm of poison gas, everyone knows it. Due to time constraints, I cannot say more about it here. I can only briefly describe the fierce situation of incendiary bombs.

Incendiary bombs range in size from the same as hand grenades to weighing two to twenty kilograms. Depending on the purpose of use, some do not ignite upon contact, while others ignite only after a certain period of time. When they ignite, they can emit high heat of over three thousand degrees, and even objects such as steel can be melted immediately. The burning time can reach as long as fifteen minutes, and the spreading range can reach one hundred square meters, and it cannot be extinguished with water.

Today's bombers already have a carrying capacity of two thousand kilograms. If they are fully loaded with incendiary bombs weighing twelve kilograms each, they can carry at least one hundred and fifty. Flying over our cities, they can immediately destroy our prosperous streets and cause one hundred and fifty fires. If the attacking enemy airplanes are two, they can cause three hundred fires. Assuming that one-third of their impact points fail to hit, they can still cause fires in two hundred places. At this time, no matter how hard the fire brigade works and how sufficient the fire trucks are, they will be overwhelmed and unable to rescue. Moreover, when roads and bridges are destroyed at the same time, houses collapse, and communication lines are cut off, the fire trucks will be unable to function due to impaired mobility and communication, and the property and lives of the citizens will only be left to be destroyed by the fire. (To be continued)

Sports News

Next Year's Berlin World Games

Astonishingly Grand Venue Construction

Construction Cost of 10 Million Marks

Hitler Considers this Great Sporting Event

Related to the Dignity of the National Government

(National Telegram from Berlin, 14th) The immensely grand venue for next year's Berlin World Games is currently under construction. Many workers are actively working to ensure the completion of this great construction on time. The construction plan is entirely the idea of ​​the Führer Hitler. Since taking power, he has opposed repairing the original sports field. This field was originally built for the 1916 Games but was ultimately not held due to the European War.

Overview of Various Construction Plans

The current new plan is to completely eliminate the original construction, using only the foundations left behind. The new plan not only involves building a large sports field on the original site, but also building a large open grassland connected to the sports field for preliminary opening ceremonies, surrounded by large grandstands. There will also be an open-air theater, an independent large swimming pool, a cycling track, a large tennis court, twelve fields for football and hockey, and two elliptical tracks for practice. There will also be a small lake for swimming practice. Only the original sports hall in one corner will be preserved without demolition. A total of six state-of-the-art sports halls will be used for fencing and other indoor sports competitions. In addition to the above-mentioned tracks, grandstands, stables, water towers, etc., new roads leading to the sports field will be built, and two railway stations and underground stations will be built near the sports field to meet future transportation needs.

Astonishing Number of Spectators

The various constructions are all incomparably grand. The large sports field can accommodate 100,000 spectators, and the open grassland for the opening ceremony can accommodate 400,000 people. After the closing ceremony, this large grassland will be used for ordinary competitions. On the main grandstand around this large grassland, a "Hitler Tower" with a height of 60 meters will be built. In addition, there will be four high buildings, below which are the entrances and exits to the large grassland. The open-air theater can accommodate 20,000 people, the tennis court and swimming pool each 10,000 people, the cycling track grandstand 15,000 people, the race track 7,000 people, and each stable can accommodate 100 horses.

Construction Cost of 10 Million Marks

This great project is estimated to cost 10 million marks, part of which is subsidized by the government, and the rest comes from various sports associations. In order to raise this huge sum, a special tax is levied on tickets for various sports competitions. According to expert observations, 10 million marks may still be insufficient. However, funding is not a problem, because the government authorities and Hitler himself consider this great sporting event to be directly related to the dignity of the country and the government. Regardless of time or financial resources, they will do everything possible to make this great sporting event a success and unparalleled.
