Grains: Flour Futures Rebound, Results Average

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, prices for all months showed a pattern of first falling, then rising, and then leveling off. The quoted prices for foreign wheat were down about 9.10 to 1.30 yuan in Chicago and 0.20 to 0.60 yuan in Canada. When the prices opened, the weakness of market sentiment due to the sharp fall in foreign wheat was expected. Therefore, the opening prices for all months fell by 0.12 yuan. However, the magnitude of the decline in foreign wheat was not significant, which was then influenced by rumors that there would be additional taxes on foreign wheat and that some mills would have to reduce production. Therefore, in the second session, the market reversed and showed an upward trend. The closing prices for the near months were similar to the previous day, while the distant months rose by an additional 0.01 yuan, indicating significant fluctuations. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, the trend had eased, and transactions had decreased. It is estimated that 400,000 to 500,000 bags were traded in the morning, and about 200,000 bags were traded in the afternoon. The output of the mills was about 200,000 to 300,000 bags, and the good-to-flat trend in the afternoon was due to the large output of the mills. Considering the subsequent trend, the price of foreign wheat may still be flat or weak. In the end, prices for January and February remained unchanged, March was up 0.075 yuan, April was up 0.005 yuan, May was unchanged, and June was up 0.075 yuan.

Wheat: Spot Month Lower, Distant Months Higher

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning, prices for all months were first flat and then stable. The quoted prices for foreign wheat were down 0.90 to 1.23 yuan in Chicago and 0.20 to 0.60 yuan in Canada. Transactions were active in the spot month at the opening, and the opening prices were down by 0.03 to 0.05 yuan. The prices for the distant months were initially flat, but then the market sentiment improved due to the rebound in the flour market and rumors of additional taxes on foreign wheat, and the prices were up by 0.02 to 0.03 yuan. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, the trend for the spot month was flat, with little fluctuation. The prices for the distant months were slightly better due to the decrease in selling. However, the rumors were not fully believed, so buying was not very active. In the end, the price for the spot month fell by 0.03 yuan, February was up 0.05 yuan, March was up 0.02 yuan, and April was up 0.05 yuan. The spot wheat market also declined, down 0.08 to 0.10 yuan from the beginning of the week. Dongguide Suzhou wheat was quoted at 3.91 yuan, second grade at 3.90 yuan, Yaowan wheat at 3.89 yuan, and Henan wheat at 3.84 yuan. A total of 8,000 bags were reportedly purchased by Fuxin.

The weakness of Chicago wheat prices today is due to the failure of Winnipeg prices to hold up. This will be reflected again in the local market, but it is not expected to be as heavy as today's selling.

River Rice Surges, Continues to Fall by 0.10 to 0.20 Yuan

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, because the sources from various provinces were quiet, more than 60 boats (totaling over 10,000 shi) were blocked, market sentiment was increasingly discouraged, and sales were stagnant. Although the Weihaiwei province brokers continued to sell 700 to 800 bags, the surge in goods ultimately made supply exceed demand, the situation continued to weaken, and the market continued to decline. Prices repeatedly fell, such as various late rice varieties down 0.10 to 0.15 yuan, and various thick japonica varieties down 0.20 yuan. Duyangjian also fell by about 0.10 yuan, and Yinbianyuan and currency softening were also observed by about 0.10 yuan. (North Shanghai) Yesterday, 20 to 30 boats of goods arrived from the river region. Sales of various types of rice in the market were slow. White japonica, Yangdu, Bukejian, Daixian, Bianyuan were slightly better in price. Thin rice and early rice were flat. White japonica prices were slightly down 0.10 to 0.20 yuan. Yangdu, Jianbianyuan, thin rice, and early rice were down by nearly 0.10 yuan.

Imported Rice Rebounds by 0.10 Yuan

Two New Ships Arrive with Confirmed Orders

Yesterday, the imported rice market opened higher in the morning due to the news of soaring prices in Saigon and Siam the previous night. Market sentiment was boosted, hoarders were determined not to sell, and new hoarders took the opportunity to buy. The appetite in the inland areas of this street was particularly strong. Inland buyers purchased 4,600 bags of Siamese broken rice, and local buyers purchased 3,000 bags of Saigon rice. Prices gradually rose by about 0.10 yuan. The return of futures rice decreased, with only 100 tons opened for each of March, April, and May. Foreign firms sold 1,000 tons for January and February, and prices rebounded by 0.10 yuan and several points. The market situation was excellent yesterday, and local buyers were very eager. The market may need to be rebuilt. However, confirmed orders are gradually arriving in Shanghai. Two new ships arrived yesterday and are docked at Yitaixing Wharf for unloading. The total is about 100,000 bags. It is estimated that another one or two ships will arrive in the next few days. Confirmed orders for December and January may need to arrive before the Lunar New Year. The customer xian rice market had been flat and weak, but yesterday, it was boosted by imported rice by 0.02 yuan. Local and inland buyers purchased 3,500 bags. Sugar Market: Guangdong Coarse Raw Sugar White Offered by Tender

Price: 18.70 Yuan

Yesterday, the sugar market trend remained flat and weak. The guild's classified two-four coarse raw sugar white, ordinary spot goods, was priced at 18.85 yuan, down another 0.05 yuan from the previous day. The first batch of 800 yuan of Guangdong sugarcane-made coarse raw sugar white that arrived previously was sold yesterday by the Sugar Industry Cooperative Company through tender, with a price of 18.70 yuan, which was 0.15 yuan lower than the price of Dutch goods. The current price of Dutch red sugar Nos. 8 and 9 was 13.90 yuan. Taikoo Sugar B mark was 19.25 yuan, also down 0.05 yuan from the previous day. The market for locally produced cotton white was stable, with No. 1 at 18.30 yuan, No. 2 at 18.10 yuan, No. 3 at 17.95 yuan, and No. 4 at 17.85 yuan. The price of Chaoqing sugar was heard to be turning flat at the place of production, while the local market was slightly quiet, and firms were watching cautiously with little progress. The quoted prices remained the same, resulting in a lack of transactions.

Metals: Strapped Iron Users Panic

In addition to the original box of prime number (ie single and double linked) and deputy number (ie company iron) tinplate, there is another kind of strapped iron, so its price is cheaper than the original box. Users are more than happy to trade because of its low price. In recent years, due to the large iron boxes made by the cigarette company, most of them are used here, so its sales have been advancing rapidly. However, this year, after the exchange rate of the shilling and the US dollar has tended to rise, overseas prices have been rising. Fellow traders have made the difference that the cost is very small compared with the genuine goods, so most of them have abandoned the strapped iron and ordered the genuine goods. The source is getting less and less day by day. In recent days, its circulating goods have even been cut off, so users have been panicking. The standard opening price for each bundle has risen to 25 yuan (calculated as 200 pounds), which is about 1 yuan better than before. I heard that the price of No. 2 goods is 29.5 yuan (200 pounds of American company iron), and the price of No. 1 goods is 33 yuan (90 pounds of double-linked American tinplate). Because of this, users have to switch to using No. 2 goods. It is heard that there will be one or two new batches of goods arriving this month, so users are trying to throw them in. It is heard that more than 40 tons have been opened, and the price is estimated to be 26.25 yuan per bundle, which is 0.75 yuan higher than before.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Discussions

Students Studying in Japan and Expelled Overseas Chinese

— Meng Ruo

Recently, the number of Chinese students studying in Japan has gradually increased. It is said that the reason is that in addition to the decrease in the Sino-Japanese exchange rate, the relationship between China and Japan has gradually become harmonious to some extent. This has to be said to be a very good phenomenon. Because the relationship between China and Japan has gradually become harmonious, the future of Sino-Japanese friendship can be optimistic. On the other hand, Chinese students who aspire to make progress can also take this opportunity to study in the East with peace of mind.

However, things in the world are always so comical. Recently, newspapers have been publishing news about the increasing number of Chinese students studying in Japan on the one hand, and news about Chinese overseas Chinese who have been expelled from Japan and have arrived in Shanghai on the other hand. Moreover, as of today (the 14th), there have been as many as 26 batches of Chinese overseas Chinese who have been expelled from Japan and returned to China. It is also heard that those who will return in succession after the 26th batch will be the 27th batch, the 28th batch, and so on.

I am putting these two things here丨students studying in Japan and refugees returning to China丨together for comparison, not to say that the reason why overseas Chinese in Japan are being expelled is because of the increase in the number of students studying in Japan; or that the reason why the number of students studying in Japan is increasing is the result of the expulsion of overseas Chinese in Japan. What I don't understand is; since the relationship between China and Japan has gradually become harmonious, it is natural for the number of students studying in Japan to increase; but why are overseas Chinese in Japan being expelled back to China? Is it that the harmony between China and Japan can only benefit students studying abroad, while overseas Chinese have to suffer instead? If there were no fact that the number of students studying in Japan is gradually increasing as proof, just looking at the expulsion of overseas Chinese in Japan back to China, we would not only not dare to believe that the relationship between China and Japan has become harmonious, but even suspect that the relationship between China and Japan is becoming increasingly broken.

However, there is no fact without a reason in the world. After trying hard to find the reason for these two things, I finally suddenly realized. It turns out that so-called students studying abroad and so-called overseas Chinese, although they are both Chinese, they are two different kinds of people. What is the difference between them? It is here; students studying abroad are consumers who bring many, many shiny silver dollars from their motherland to spend in Japan; overseas Chinese are producers who sometimes inevitably remit some Japanese currency back to their motherland to settle down. The former kind of people are beneficial to the Japanese, while the latter kind of people are harmful to the Japanese.

This is the reason why the Japanese welcome our students studying abroad and expel our overseas Chinese.

Japanese Ronin Open Pawnshops and Pawn Young Girls

— Liang

According to a recent report from Tianjin, many pawnshops opened by Japanese ronin in Tangshan are exploiting people with high interest rates. On the 13th, a refugee couple from Yutian, carrying a daughter, only twenty years old, with a very beautiful appearance, had no travel expenses to leave the customs. They were seen by the owner of a Japanese pawnshop who induced them to pawn the girl for one month for 20 yuan, with a monthly interest of 2 yuan. There was a contract stating that when redeeming the girl, they must also repay the expenses for food and drink, etc. This piece of news is a unique innovation in the pawnshop industry. It can be seen that the Japanese's exploitation with high interest rates and whimsical ideas are truly meticulous. Although this matter is very small,

Page 22

the impact of its occurrence is very significant. I wonder, if the parents of a male lacked travel expenses, would he also be pawned? If only females are pawned and not males, what is the reason for this? If an old woman lacks travel expenses, would she also be pawned? If only young girls are pawned and not old women, what is the reason for this?

Just speaking of young girls, I have several feelings: (1) The pawnshop publicly accepts young girls as pledges, treating young girls as the same as goods, and their psychology of despising Chinese people can be expressed. (2) Charging 2 yuan in interest for one month, if pawned for one year, it must be 24 yuan, which means the interest rate is higher than the principal. (3) Even in one month, the interest is already 2 yuan. If food and drink expenses are added, and the price is not specified, it can be extorted at will. Even if the asking price is not too high, the cost of food and drink for one month must be 4 or 5 yuan, so how can the pawner have the ability to redeem the girl? (4) The pawnee is also a mature and beautiful woman. If the shop owner is unscrupulous and violates her chastity, how should this account be settled?

Therefore, I believe that this kind of fact is nominally accepting young girls as pledges, but in reality, it is selling young girls, because, on the one hand, with such a high interest rate, the pawner will definitely not be able to redeem the girl, and on the other hand, a young and beautiful woman entering the shop has no absolute guarantee. However, taking a further step to explore the essence of this matter, it lies in the fact that our country's wealthy compatriots do not show compassion for their fellow countrymen in difficulty and do not try to find ways to help them. Therefore, they have no choice but to be manipulated by Japanese ronin. The blame does not lie with the Japanese, so why blame the Japanese?

Wanderer

— Hui

The pale light of the gas lamp flickered at the corner of the alley. Raindrops, under that white light, scattered down like broken glass. It was already about eleven o'clock. There was still the sound of a car horn or two on the road, but that sound was very muffled, almost inaudible in this quiet, deep alley. At this time, Li Ada was still lying alone in a corner under that pale light, panting weakly. Gusts of wind mixed with raindrops hit his body, and his teeth chattered, his body constantly trembling. Although he wanted to get up and move around, his limbs, which had no strength, could not be lifted no matter how hard he struggled. It seemed that something weighing a thousand catties was pressing down, making it impossible to move even a little.

Li Ada had been sick for the past few days. It was originally a very minor illness, but it seemed like a serious illness to him. His hungry stomach and cold body made his illness even more severe. He repeatedly wanted to take some medicine, but he could not find any money no matter how he tried. Yesterday, he was so hungry that he could no longer bear it. He tried his best to walk, but in the end, he only got two rotten buns from Lin Mazi, and he has been like this until now. Although he had been dizzy from hunger several times and his whole body was stiff from the cold, he could no longer get up.

At this time, his eyes blurred as he looked at the pale light of the gas lamp. His face, covered with a layer of black dust, looked even paler. His breathing gradually became weaker, and the faces of his mother and younger brother, who had starved to death during the great drought this year, appeared in his mind. His weak nerves suddenly felt a heat like fire, and he passed out unconsciously.

Li Ada was originally a farmer. He was known for his honesty in the village. Although he was only in his twenties this year, he had been hired to work as a farmhand since his father died when he was fourteen. For more than ten years in a row, he had never rested. But this year, there was a great drought everywhere. Although Li Ada was honest and reliable, no one hired him to work as a farmhand. His mother, who worked as a maid for others, was also fired. His fifteen-year-old younger brother also stopped doing small business. The three of them were living on loans every day. At first, the villagers lent them some money because they were all honest people, but gradually, they borrowed too much, and others had no way to help them. The three of them had no choice but to endure hunger. At this time, his younger brother became ill. This illness was entirely caused by hunger, but as a result, he died from the illness. His fifty-year-old mother fell ill and died less than ten days later, partly because his younger brother had died and partly because she could not bear the hunger. At this time, Li Ada could no longer live in this village, so he and Lin Mazi and a few others from the village went to the metropolis of Shanghai together. But after arriving here, none of the five or six of them could find a way to make a living, and they ended up wandering the streets all day, becoming a group of homeless wanderers.

(Hey, Ada, get up, I've been looking for you for a long time, but you're lying here.)

Li Ada vaguely heard someone calling him. He slowly and weakly opened his dull eyes. At this time, he realized that he had not died yet. Lin Mazi was sitting next to him, shivering.

(Are you hungry? Brother Liu San is coming soon. He went to find a way, let's wait for him to bring something for you to eat!)

Lin Mazi said with his teeth chattering, but in Li Ada's view, he was afraid that he would no longer have the good fortune to eat something brought by Liu San. He looked at Lin Mazi with a bitter face, moaning without saying a word.

Time was passing quickly. It was almost dawn. Although the rain had stopped, the northwest wind was even colder when it blew on people. At this time, Liu San and Liu Er, the two brothers, walked in from outside the alley, but when the two of them got closer, they only saw Lin Mazi staring blankly and shedding tears. The pale light of the gas lamp shone on his face, which was just white, with no blood at all. He saw the two of them coming and said in a low voice:

(We have lost another companion.)

When Liu San and Liu Er heard these words, they looked at Li Ada, who was lying in the corner and could no longer move, and stood silently.

Foreign Land

— Qin

About three or forty years ago, people thought that foreign lands were barren lands. However, as the number of overseas Chinese who made fortunes in Southeast Asia increased day by day, people envied foreign lands as if they were golden heavens.

When I was a child, I ate the "foreign cakes" brought back by returning overseas Chinese, and I saw them wearing black silk shirts and pants. How beautiful and lovely the foreign land was! These dream traces were deeply imprinted in my heart. But I didn't know that "foreign land" (鄉俗意指南洋) -- local customs refer to Southeast Asia -- was originally similar to a place inhabited by barbarians. All of them were Southern Chinese who went there at the risk of their lives, and gradually developed it. In the beginning, shipping was not yet very developed, and sea routes were not yet open. People from Guangdong and Fujian, with their adventurous and brave nature, boldly sailed on large wooden boats that were very easy to sink. The number of people who died midway, and those who died in foreign lands due to acclimatization and the difficulty of living in the barbarian land, is truly unknown. Even twenty years ago, when there were more people in my hometown who were considered to have gone abroad, it was still regarded as a terrible and unfamiliar place! The children of wealthy families were reluctant to let him go abroad. Most of them were prodigal sons who were not very tolerated in their hometowns, so they had to go abroad. Even in the most prosperous times of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, people who went abroad were still very hard.

Leaving their hometowns, abandoning their wives and children, and going abroad, in the eyes of Chinese people who have the deepest sense of belonging to their homeland, is the most desolate thing. Just take the closer Vietnam as an example. Finding nearly twenty yuan for travel expenses also requires more than ten yuan for the entrance fee, and it is even more necessary to prepare to pay the first year's head tax of more than thirty yuan. This large capital for going abroad is often borrowed with great difficulty; some even sell oxen, marry widowed sisters-in-law, or sell daughters, and want to go to foreign lands to make a living, leaving behind their families and relatives in their hometown, with their hearts full of sadness. When they arrive at the seaside, they see the endless green water rolling and rolling.

Those Who Don't Recognize Treasure

Page 23

These are mostly new immigrants from the countryside, and their hearts are already sour with sadness.

Finally, the ship crossed the Seven Seas, and the seawater changed from green to black, and then from black back to green. If the voyage is smooth, they have already suffered a lot of hardship on the journey. The life in the hold for several days and nights is certainly not pleasant.

The ship safely enters the port and arrives at the shore of the foreign land. But they cannot disembark at will. They stand on the deck and wait, being fried by the tropical sunlight. They don't know how many hours they have to wait before they are allowed to climb onto the land of the foreign land. They cannot leave freely, but must continue to wait. Luggage is not allowed to be taken away immediately, but must be taken into the luggage inspection room to be inspected. Only after all the entry procedures have been completed can they go to the luggage inspection room to retrieve it. Whether the things they retrieve are missing or not, they can only accept their fate. After being kicked and beaten, they have to spend some money to get their things back properly. This is also considered a difficult hurdle.

After putting the luggage in the luggage inspection room, people must be driven into the new guest office like pigs. If their fate is good, the officials will handle their entry procedures on the same day. They must have a merchant guarantee before they can stay. After paying all the entry papers and head tax papers, they can be released from the new guest office. Like prisoners, they have to make several fingerprints. The officials sign the papers and receive a head tax paper. This paper must be carried with them at all times, otherwise, if they are caught, they will be arrested and imprisoned first before anything else is said. If they lose it, it is the same as not having paid it, and they have to pay it again, which is expensive and very troublesome. If the ship arrives at the shore when the officials are not working, they will be locked up in the new guest office overnight, with no food or place to sleep, which is even more bitter than being in prison. When handling the procedures peacefully, it is very common to be kicked and beaten unexpectedly.

Even if they safely leave the new guest office and temporarily find a place to live, whether they can find a job is also a troubling problem. There is no need to say more about the taste of unemployment. Even if they have a job, it is not easy to be a clerk in an overseas Chinese store. There is no limit to how many hours they work. Except for the time for sleeping and eating, they almost sell themselves entirely to the boss. It is difficult to find entertainment and happiness. They only love to worry about their hometown.

In an unfamiliar place, when they are sick, the store will definitely not allow sick clerks to receive their salary for nothing. They are dismissed and sent to every hospital to wait for death. If they want to go back, they cannot leave freely. They must report to the government forty days in advance and pay several dollars for the exit paper fee. Only after it is found that there is no other reason will they be allowed to leave. A foreign land is like a strange and ruthless prison!

Personal Tragedy

— Simon

Previously, the splendid ideals and gentle dreams cherished in my mind, once struck by cruel encounters, shattered instantly, like a glass full of red wine dashed against a rock. Now, I have no fanciful thoughts at all. My only hope now is that the pair of dreadful beasts of life, constantly pursuing me, can ease up a little, stop chasing so relentlessly, allowing me to calm my panicked emotions, my wildly beating heart, to rest my weary legs, and let me catch my breath for a moment. But is this possible? No, it's not. If my legs slow down even slightly, those beast-like aspects of life will pounce on me, nearly devouring me as a snack.

Therefore, I can only struggle with the last of my strength, panting, running forward, not even daring to look back.

Life is truly like a ferocious beast! It constantly instills in me all sorts of fears and threats, glaring at me with vicious eyes, waiting for me to slip up and finish me off. Because of this, I have to support my frail body day after day, from dawn till late at night, crouching in a musty and narrow little room, ruthlessly taxing my brain to its utmost, spreading out the manuscript paper, line after line transferring from my mind to the tip of my pen, and from the tip of my pen scratching onto the paper.

Ah, the one who consumes his own heart's blood; having set down his pen, he sighs in this way.

My mind is so weary that I must lie down, but I still have to force open my tired, watering eyelids and continue to smear words on the paper, one by one. Sometimes, even when sick, I still have to bear the pain of illness and work on the manuscript, unless my eyes see flowers and my head is dizzy. Whenever I finish a piece of writing and read it again from the beginning, my heart inevitably aches terribly, as if suddenly struck heavily by an iron hammer. Within it are countless traces of my own fresh red blood and mottled tears! Often, in the quiet of late at night, under the lamplight, I would take out many of my stored manuscripts, casually flipping through them, and sometimes I would recall a ridiculous state of mind from earlier days. At that time, I used to regard them as a place of spiritual respite, as the ultimate source of my soul's refuge, even as the only companion on the lonely journey of life. I treasured them in my luggage, like a cherished object, accompanying me through many places, for a long time, almost unwilling to part with them. In lonely inns, unable to dispel the long nights, I would often open my luggage and take them out, happily admiring them, feeling that these were the crystallizations of my soul's flowers, possessing infinite glory. And so, a wonderful feeling of solace would slowly fill my entire heart, almost intoxicating me with this spiritual comfort. But this ridiculous state of mind had long since vanished along with my dreams and ideals.

How is it now? When I look at them, my hands tremble, my heart aches, and I am filled with anger, seeing them as the greatest enemies of my life, no longer a spiritual refuge, a companion in life. Within them, so many of my bloodstains, so many of my tearstains, have been rendered. They are like a poisonous worm, invisibly gnawing away at my youth, devouring my life. What emotions are left? I only have pain, hatred, loathing. When my hatred reaches its extreme, I almost want to light a fire and burn them all to ashes, so they will never appear before my eyes again, because as soon as I see them, I will inevitably and naturally recall the past, feeling that things have changed too quickly, and I will feel infinite sorrow.

The glory that exists for people like me, especially when I see others' fervent praise for me, or the comfort and joy of seeing my own work, does not exist for me in the slightest. I only know that with each session of writing on paper, a little more of my heart's blood is poured out, and at the same time, my life takes another step closer to the edge of the grave. Therefore, I have no hope at all that when my eyes are closed and my breathing stops, someone will come to my tomb, reciting my poems while proclaiming my deeds during my lifetime. I only hope to be able to part with those things forever, or perhaps live a little longer, but this unknown tragedy will not end until the very last day.

Storytelling

Yao Xiaoan Wang Pingqiu Qilin Bao

China West (1040) 11:00 PM to 12:00 AM

Opening (Nine Sons Reciting a Child)

Nine sons born of one mother, and also a daughter with red makeup. Returning to the court with much glory, the gatekeeper rushes to report to the inner hall. The madam, hearing the news, hurries out to greet him, welcoming the husband to the inner hall. Madam, I was made emperor abroad for thirteen years, hoping that you have been safe and well. I don't know which of the nine sons is the best; I hope you will tell me about their deeds one by one. Husband, the eldest son is a first-rank official serving as prime minister; the second son is a successful candidate seated in the main hall. The third son is enfeoffed as a earl in Yunnan; the fourth son is the Minister of War. The fifth son is the governor of Shandong; the sixth son teaches the crown prince literature in the East Palace. The Left Deputy Censor-in-Chief is the seventh son; the Minister of Personnel is the eighth son. Although the ninth son is young, he was the top scorer in the imperial examination last year. The one daughter is sixteen years old; the emperor selected her to be a consort. The nine daughters-in-law are all virtuous; eight granddaughters accompany her in the embroidery room. The twelve grandsons are skilled in both literature and martial arts; each studies literature in the study, and can also engage in duels with swords and spears in their free time. Twenty years ago, I received a sign: gauze hats and red robes filled the hall, moreover, a golden dragon hung in the center. Now, the nine sons recite grandsons, possessing wealth and honor; each of the nine beauties has much glory. Descendants fill the hall, and children and grandchildren flourish.

Li Yanqiu, Legend of the White Snake

Yuan Chang (1120) 11:30 PM to 12:15 AM

Opening (Baoyu Becomes a Monk)

Settling the graves, going to Jinling. A lone boat breaks through the waves. Boundless beauty for ten thousand miles, sky and water in sight open up the chest. By the side of the village, two or three have no vulgarity, at which forest scenery poetic and edible deep. The waves lap the sides of the boat, gusts of fresh wind carry the homeward journey. Thinking of the letters from home with such strange words, how is it that Baoyu has not returned home safe and sound? Heart ash, intention sinking, truly an unfortunate family, as it has been said since ancient times. That day, braving the rain, came to Kun Bi Ling Station, how could the wind and thunder meet, unable to proceed. Jia Zheng unintentionally peered out of the window, at leisure. Suddenly, he saw a poor monk walking along the riverbank. He was bald, barefoot, in tattered clothes, standing against the wind, unable to bear the cold. His face seemed familiar, but he could not recall it in his heart. From afar, he repeatedly bowed towards the boat, clasping his hands, bowing and greeting. Suddenly, he remembered that the missing Baoyu was him. Why shave your head and enter the emptiness? (Crying) Son, the old ancestor's love was not false, leaving without saying goodbye is too unbearable. Nineteen years of nurturing cannot be repaid, thinking of such an ending, is it not even more heartbreaking? As a father, I will go home today, come and travel together in the same boat. Baoyu is silent, without a sound, like joy, like sorrow, sighing, tears streaming, without words answering the elderly. Suddenly, two monks and Daoists came to drag Yu away, in an instant, the person and shadow disappeared. Hurriedly chasing, unable to catch up, father and son ultimately do not come close to each other, leaving only vague footprints in the snow.

Ms. Wang Bingmei Tang Poetry

Hua Xing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Staying Overnight at Master Ye's Mountain Cottage, Especially Missing Great and Not Coming - Meng Haoran

The setting sun passes the western ridge, the flock of birds suddenly darkens.

Pine moon brings the night's coolness, wind spring fills clear listening.

Woodcutters return, their desire ends, smoke birds settle initially.

You who are scheduled to stay overnight, my lonely zither awaits by the ivy path.

Playing with the Moon in the Southern Study with My Younger Cousin, Remembering Vice-Prefect Cui of Shanyin and Wang Changling

Sleeping in the southern study, I opened the curtain as the moon emerged.

Clear light washes over the water and trees, rippling in the window.

How many times the waxing and waning, clarity transforms in the ancient and modern.

A beautiful woman by the clear riverbank, sighs in the night, the Yue tune bitter.

A thousand miles, how is it? A gentle breeze blows on the orchid and Du Ruo grass.

Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao Local Edition - Film Special Edition

Claudette Colbert's Correspondence with a Unique Fan (Part 1)

— Ti Yun

Is it possible? Can a star and a fan develop a special relationship? Most people who enjoy watching movies like to correspond with their favorite movie stars. But what about the stars themselves? Do they pick out one or two special people from among the thousands of fans and develop special feelings for them? Do they pick out a few special and different letters from among the thousands of fan letters, which occupy a special and superior place in the hearts of the stars?

According to ordinary facts, it is almost impossible. No matter how touching your letter is, it is just one among thousands. Some are special and different from ordinary fan letters, but the number of letters received every day is so large, and the stars have never met you, so how can they develop special feelings for you? However, Claudette Colbert is an exception to the rule. She has a sincerely beloved fan.

Once, she was talking to a newspaper reporter. At first, she seemed eager to tell him about it. But then she shook her head frequently. How could she be embarrassed to say it? She suddenly gave people a surprise. She suddenly looked up and laughed loudly. After a while, she quickly apologized, saying, "Please forgive me. Every time I think about how this thing started, I can't help but laugh. At the beginning, I didn't find it interesting. I felt very angry, but now... I can't help but laugh when I think about it."

"What's his name?" the reporter asked.

Claudette stared at the reporter, unable to answer for a moment. She suddenly pursed her lips, revealing a mischievous smile. Then she suddenly jumped up and ran out of the reception room. After a while, she came back with a large package of letters. She smiled and sat down, untied the green gauze ribbon around the letters, and then said, "I know that person very well. Even if I announced his name, he wouldn't necessarily blame me. She said, taking out the first letter, "You can see for yourself."

The reporter read the letter. The name signed was Daniel Kirk, a man's name. Inside, the fan sent Claudette Colbert a movie script. Of course, Claudette didn't have time to read scripts sent by strangers. She set this rule, instructing her secretary that if someone sent a script from outside, there was no need to notify her, just write a thank-you note and return it. This time, her secretary broke the rule and took the fan's letter and the movie script he wrote to her to read. Claudette had worked hard all day that day and was in a bad mood. Hearing her words, she immediately jumped up and scolded her secretary, saying that she didn't understand the rules. But her secretary said that the script was particularly good. This made Claudette even angrier. She threw the script on the ground and drove her secretary out.

After her secretary left, she unintentionally picked up the script and flipped through it. On the last page, she found a line of small print, which read, "I don't know if Miss Colbert will read this, who knows?" Claudette went to her desk and wrote him a letter herself. There were no other words on it, only the three words "Who knows?" After she finished writing, she attached the letter to the script and returned it to Mr. Kirk. She thought that everything was over this time.

But after a few days, she received another letter from the fan, which only contained three similar words, "God knows."

Claudette found these three words very interesting and very simple. She then wrote another reply in passing, which read, "Does God really exist?" A few days later, she received another reply, which contained only one word, "Doubter."

Claudette was happy for a moment and replied to him with another letter, which said, "You claim to be a writer, which is really a boast." (After "Doubter," she forgot to put a period to end the sentence.) (To be continued)

Film Commentary

Review of (New Love, Old Love)

— Ling He

Blinddate 丨 Cathay

In the minds of American filmmakers, love between men and women is often very mysterious, transcending economic or any other boundaries. Rich young masters will marry poor women, and young men from working-class backgrounds often receive the favor of noble ladies. The conclusion is that love is originally mysterious and incredible. And this is also the main thing expressed in their works. But what we usually see is not like this. Regarding this point, I remember that in the British production (The Way to Independence), it was explained very clearly that the temporary love between the factory owner's son and the female worker does exist, for a temporary need, but between them, because of the difference in economy and status, they cannot be combined after all.

However, we will not ignore their concept of such creation. For example, in this (New Love, Old Love), the playwright fully expresses the rich young man's benevolence, generously purchasing expensive clothing for her, and he heavily supports the lover and those she cares for. This caters to the general psychology of climbing up, and its role in lying is too obvious.

Judging from this, how should (New Love, Old Love) be evaluated? There is no need to explain further, but in terms of the image of expression, there are quite a few lovely places here. For example, writing about Katie's family, her younger siblings are constantly arguing, and the personalities of her father and mother are so active. Those characters are really too typical of old-fashioned families. This gives people simple laughter, and because of such a lovely performance, it gives people a lot of good feelings.

All the actors are very dedicated, especially those who play the mother and father are even better. Extraordinary skills express ordinary content.

The Central Film Studio, sponsored by the Film Division of the Central Party Headquarters in Nanjing, is conducting a large-scale search for male and female actors in Shanghai, Nanjing, and Beijing for the needs of preparing to produce films. Applicants are not restricted by age or qualifications. Anyone who feels interested in film art and is confident that they can achieve considerable success has the hope of being selected. Once selected, their lives will be guaranteed with extreme safety, and they will be able to give full play to their personal talents under the cultivation of the state. Submission Guidelines for the *Shenbao* Film Supplement

This publication is a film journal dedicated to promoting culture and art. We welcome submissions from external sources. Once published, compensation will be generous.

Once the text is published and compensation is given, the copyright belongs to the *Shenbao*.

The language of this publication is primarily vernacular Chinese and must use modern punctuation.

Each submission must be stamped with a seal; otherwise, it will be considered unpaid.

Due to limited space, articles should be concise, ideally around 500 characters.

If the submission is a translation, please include the original text. Avoid mixing in English where possible. Unless stated in advance and accompanied by a self-addressed stamped envelope, we are not responsible for preserving or returning texts, photos, etc.

Do not write on both sides of the paper, write horizontally, or use a pencil.

If duplicate submissions, plagiarized content, or copied descriptions are discovered, no compensation will be provided.

Film Novel

Meeting Again Awaiting Marriage (Forsaking All Others) (6)

— Su Yin

Geoffrey said, "He sent me a telegram saying he got married last night." Mary's lips trembled, but she forced a smile and said, "He... he must have said he was sorry to me in the telegram, right?" Geoffrey nodded, "Yes." Mary said, "That's good. At least he has a conscience to send me a telegram. Poor Deron, no matter where he is, he always remembers me." Eleanor felt sorry for her and asked her to sit down and rest for a while. But Mary, with a pitiable voice, said, "Why sit down? The bride should be standing. Have you ever seen a bride sitting down to get married? It's not proper! It's not proper to sit down to get married! You should stand in front of the altar. And after the wedding is over! You also have to kiss the groom. But now there's no groom to kiss! He's already married Connie Barnes..." Her voice! became louder and louder. Finally, she covered her head with her hands and cried.

After this, Mary spent many miserable days. She moved to a rural area, lived in a wooden house, swam in the lake, rode horses, and exhausted herself to the extreme, unable to sleep at night. She knew she had to forget everything in the past. There was no point in having her heart beat for a stone. In this way, after some time, her broken heart gradually healed, and she gradually felt the beauty of the sunset without Deron's presence, and she gradually felt the pleasure of cold water on her yellow skin, and she gradually understood what it meant to live alone and be healthy.

Later, Geoffrey and Herbert also came, which made her even happier. Geoffrey also brought many letters. After dinner, they gathered together to open the letters, all four of them: Mary, Paula, Geoffrey, and Herbert. Mary suddenly held a letter in her hand and said to Geoffrey, "Geoffrey, listen to this;" She then read the letter: "After a long separation, we are planning to reunite. We will be waiting for you for tea at the Xizun residence at 9 pm on the 8th of this month. We hope you will grace us with your presence." Below it was signed "Connie. Deron Linda." Geoffrey listened and only replied with a grunt. But Mary said, "The 8th is the day after tomorrow. The first thing I need to do tomorrow when I go to the city is to get my hair done. The second thing is..." Geoffrey felt strange and said, "Mary... do you want to go?" Mary said, "Of course, I'll go." Geoffrey stood up, walked to Mary, sat down on a small stool at her feet, and then said, "Mary, are you confused? You must not know what that means. That woman just wants to humiliate you. You're not at all prepared for that kind of thing. Don't fall for her tricks." But Mary shook her head and said, "I don't think Connie wants me to go. But we're going anyway. See what she looks like, okay? Besides, I'm already healed, I can't even remember what Deron's eyes look like, whether he has a nose or not. What am I afraid of them?"

On that day, Mary indeed went to Deron's residence with Geoffrey. She met Deron in the garden after dinner. They strolled together, and soft music wafted over, and dim lights in the room were scattered on the ground. Mary had no defenses. Deron suddenly embraced Mary, kissing her fiercely, recounting his love to her again and again, and admitting his mistakes and present regrets. Mary pushed him away, but Deron refused to let her go. He pleaded, "Mary, you must listen to me. Now there's no point in talking about who's right and who's wrong. The only question now is that I have always loved you..." Just as they were in this difficult situation, Connie suddenly appeared. Obviously, she had a pre-arranged plan, which was... (To be continued)

Cuiwei Peak in Ningdu, Jiangxi, is extremely steep. Only this cave can lead to the top of the peak. The terrain is so dangerous that one man can hold the pass against ten thousand. When Zhu and Mao were trapped in Ningdu, a small number of residents fled to the top of the peak and resisted. All of them died heroically. Their nature was extremely tragic.

It is said that most diseases are a manifestation of imbalance in the organs. This difference, that is, the unhealthy phenomenon in the human body, can be analyzed by hydrolyzing the fluid in the organs and cells of animals to find out what kind of secretion is lacking. The experimental results are very effective, attracting great attention in the world's medical and pharmaceutical circles. The picture shows the extraction of secretions from patients with equipment for analysis to determine the injection of certain fluids.
